<p><i><b>Christina Aguilera</b></i> is the self-titled debut <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio album</a> by American singer <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>. It was released on August 24, 1999, by <a href="/wiki/RCA_Records" title="RCA Records">RCA Records</a>. After recording "<a href="/wiki/Reflection_(song)" title="Reflection (song)">Reflection</a>", the theme song for <i><a href="/wiki/Mulan_(1998_film)" title="Mulan (1998 film)">Mulan</a></i>, RCA laid the foundation for the album immediately and started presenting Aguilera with tracks for her debut album, which they later decided would have a January 1999 release. Its music incorporates <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen pop</a> genres, with a few songs featuring strong elements from <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>. Contributions to the album's production came from a wide range of producers, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_Frank_(music)" title="David Frank (music)">David Frank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Fair" title="Ron Fair">Ron Fair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guy_Roche" title="Guy Roche">Guy Roche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Thicke" title="Robin Thicke">Robin Thicke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diane_Warren" title="Diane Warren">Diane Warren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Wilder" title="Matthew Wilder">Matthew Wilder</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Zigman" title="Aaron Zigman">Aaron Zigman</a>.</p>
<p><i>Christina Aguilera</i> earned Aguilera the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_New_Artist" title="Grammy Award for Best New Artist">Grammy Award for Best New Artist</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000_Grammy_Awards" title="2000 Grammy Awards">2000 Grammy Awards</a>. The release debuted at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with first-week sales of 253,000 copies. <i>Christina Aguilera</i> was <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">certified</a> octuple platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) and has sold more than 9 million copies in the US. Globally, the project has sold over 20 million units, making it one of the best selling albums worldwide.</p>
<p>The album was preceded by four <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">singles</a>. "<a href="/wiki/Genie_in_a_Bottle" title="Genie in a Bottle">Genie in a Bottle</a>" was released as the <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> from the project and peaked atop the <a href="/wiki/Record_chart" title="Record chart">record charts</a> of twenty one nations, including the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. Three subsequent singles additionally became top ten records: "<a href="/wiki/What_a_Girl_Wants_(Christina_Aguilera_song)" title="What a Girl Wants (Christina Aguilera song)">What a Girl Wants</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I_Turn_to_You_(Christina_Aguilera_song)" title="I Turn to You (Christina Aguilera song)">I Turn to You</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Come_On_Over_Baby_(All_I_Want_Is_You)" title="Come On Over Baby (All I Want Is You)">Come On Over Baby (All I Want Is You)</a>". To further promote the album, Aguilera performed on television shows and embarked on the tour <i><a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera_in_Concert" title="Christina Aguilera in Concert">Christina Aguilera in Concert</a></i> in 2000.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christina_Aguilera_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Christina Aguilera approached record label <a href="/wiki/RCA_Records" title="RCA Records">RCA</a>, then having financial difficulties, and was told to contact Disney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debut_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-debut-1">[1]</a></sup> After being given the opportunity to record the theme to the 1998 film <i><a href="/wiki/Mulan_(1998_film)" title="Mulan (1998 film)">Mulan</a></i> named "<a href="/wiki/Reflection_(song)" title="Reflection (song)">Reflection</a>" it was reported she had gained a record deal with RCA Records with Aguilera saying "I landed a record deal simultaneously as I landed the <i>Mulan</i> soundtrack. I had just turned seventeen years old, and during the same week, I just landed both. I recorded the <i>Mulan</i> soundtrack first and then a few months later I was out in L.A. recording the record for about six months".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mulan_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-mulan-2">[2]</a></sup> When asked about the song and Aguilera, RCA executive <a href="/wiki/Ron_Fair" title="Ron Fair">Ron Fair</a> commented,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"She is a badass genius of singing. She was put on this earth to sing, and I've worked with a lot of singers.... When Aguilera met with us, she didn't care that she was auditioning for a record deal; she got into a performance zone that you see in artist much more mature than she is."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>After she was asked to hit a musical note required for "Reflection", she thought that the song could be the gateway into an album deal. Aguilera spent hours recording a cover of <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Run_to_You_(Whitney_Houston_song)" title="Run to You (Whitney Houston song)">Run to You</a>", which included the note she was asked to hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debut_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-debut-1">[1]</a></sup> After successfully hitting the note, which she called "the note that changed my life", she was given the opportunity to record the song. To record the song, she flew to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> for roughly a week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-ref-4">[4]</a></sup> Despite growing increasingly exhausted during the recording sessions, when she heard that a 90-piece orchestra would be arriving to record the instrumental she begged to stay and witness the event. She later called the experience "amazing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-ref-4">[4]</a></sup> Due to the success around the recording of "Reflection", RCA wished for Aguilera to record and release an album by September 1998 to maintain the "hype" surrounding her at that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-ref-4">[4]</a></sup> The label laid the foundation for the album immediately and started presenting Aguilera with tracks for her debut album, which they later decided would have a January 1999 release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-ref-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith.2C_Andy_2007_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smith.2C_Andy_2007-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording_and_production">Recording and production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christina_Aguilera_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording and production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;max-width:302px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:174px;max-width:174px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shelly_P_in_studio.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1242" data-file-width="1701" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Shelly_P_in_studio.jpg/172px-Shelly_P_in_studio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Shelly_P_in_studio.jpg/258px-Shelly_P_in_studio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Shelly_P_in_studio.jpg/344px-Shelly_P_in_studio.jpg 2x" width="172"/></a></div>

<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:124px;max-width:124px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diane_Warren_03A.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1164" data-file-width="1132" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Diane_Warren_03A.jpg/122px-Diane_Warren_03A.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Diane_Warren_03A.jpg/183px-Diane_Warren_03A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Diane_Warren_03A.jpg/244px-Diane_Warren_03A.jpg 2x" width="122"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Shelly_Peiken" title="Shelly Peiken">Shelly Peiken</a> (left), co-wrote the hit "What a Girl Wants" and the single version of "Come on Over", while <a href="/wiki/Diane_Warren" title="Diane Warren">Diane Warren</a> (right) wrote "<a href="/wiki/I_Turn_to_You_(All-4-One_song)#Christina_Aguilera_version" title="I Turn to You (All-4-One song)">I Turn to You</a>", a cover of the <a href="/wiki/All-4-One" title="All-4-One">All-4-One</a> song, which became a hit in Aguilera's voice, and "Somebody's Somebody".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Christina Aguilera</i> was recorded between 1998 and 1999, with <a href="/wiki/Ron_Fair" title="Ron Fair">Ron Fair</a> serving as the album's <a href="/wiki/Executive_producer" title="Executive producer">executive producer</a>. The label reportedly spent $1 million on writers, producers and voice lessons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost-6">[6]</a></sup> According to Fair, "She was very much a raw talent, so building a collection of songs that would become her first album was a time-consuming process. We wanted to find the ones that could knock the door down and put her up there."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost-6">[6]</a></sup> The album was built around <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> songs, which was against Aguilera's will, since she wanted a more <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> album. She further explained during an interview for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>: "I was held back a lot from doing more R&amp;B ad-libbing. They clearly wanted to make a fresh-sounding young pop record and that's not always the direction I wanted to go in. Sometimes they didn't get it, didn't want to hear me out because of my age, and that was a little bit frustrating. Since all the success, it's a little easier to get my opinions across."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>One of the first producers of the album was <a href="/wiki/Guy_Roche" title="Guy Roche">Guy Roche</a>, who produced two tracks ("What a Girl Wants" and "I Turn to You") and co-wrote one of them ("What a Girl Wants"), along with <a href="/wiki/Shelly_Peiken" title="Shelly Peiken">Shelly Peiken</a>. "What a Girl Wants" was later re-recorded for its single release, replacing the "lighter" version for a more "funky" <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> version. Peiken also re-wrote with Roche the single version for the track "Come on Over", first produced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johan_Aberg" title="Johan Aberg">Johan Aberg</a>, Paul Rein and Aaron Zigman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-discogs_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-discogs-7">[7]</a></sup> According to herself, "We're going to give it more of an edge, R&amp;B it up a little, maybe rock it out a little, give it a lot of different new directions and get it out there."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jam_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-jam-8">[8]</a></sup> Aguilera also recorded a cover of <a href="/wiki/All-4-One" title="All-4-One">All-4-One</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/I_Turn_to_You_(All-4-One_song)#Christina_Aguilera_version" title="I Turn to You (All-4-One song)">I Turn to You</a>", written by <a href="/wiki/Diane_Warren" title="Diane Warren">Diane Warren</a>. <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sturken_and_Evan_Rogers" title="Carl Sturken and Evan Rogers">Carl Sturken and Evan Rogers</a> (who would eventually broke into the scene as the producers who launched <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>'s career) wrote and produced two tracks, while the then up-and-coming <a href="/wiki/Robin_Thicke" title="Robin Thicke">Robin Thicke</a> co-wrote and co-produced "When You Put Your Hands on Me". <a href="/wiki/Franne_Golde" title="Franne Golde">Franne Golde</a> (who previously worked with <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>) also wrote a song for Aguilera. At the final stages, producer and songwriter <a href="/wiki/David_Frank_(musician)" title="David Frank (musician)">David Frank</a> presented a song called "Genie in a Bottle",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sos_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-sos-9">[9]</a></sup> which Aguilera almost didn't record, "because there were a lot of other artists out there that were after this song, so we had to fight a little bit to get it," she claimed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-postgazette_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-postgazette-10">[10]</a></sup> With <a href="/wiki/Heather_Holley" title="Heather Holley">Heather Holley</a>, Aguilera also co-wrote a track called "I Will Be", which she said was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey_(album)" title="Mariah Carey (album)">Vanishing</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rscover_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-rscover-11">[11]</a></sup> Producer of the track "So Emotional" revealed that Aguilera in-between recordings "she was only listening to <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a>, putting on her walk man and practicing their riffs and runs, before she did her ad-libs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christina_Aguilera_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">

</div>

<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>

</table>
<p><i>Christina Aguilera</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen pop</a> album;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusicreview_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicreview-13">[13]</a></sup> it mainly consists of teen pop songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popmatters_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-popmatters-14">[14]</a></sup> Beth Johnson of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> compared the album's musical styles to those of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiffany_(American_singer)" title="Tiffany (American singer)">Tiffany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW-15">[15]</a></sup> The record opens with "<a href="/wiki/Genie_in_a_Bottle" title="Genie in a Bottle">Genie in a Bottle</a>", which uses sexual references to talk about self-respect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> editor Kenneth Partridge wrote that the song features "32nd-note bass-drum pattern that mimics the heart palpitations of a teenager in lust."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBTrackByTrack_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBTrackByTrack-17">[17]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/What_a_Girl_Wants_(Christina_Aguilera_song)" title="What a Girl Wants (Christina Aguilera song)">What a Girl Wants</a>" is a hybrid of teen pop and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> which lyrically "[reveals] an independent, strong woman who knows what she wants from a relationship, both sexually and emotionally."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IdoReview_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-IdoReview-19">[19]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">cover version</a> of <a href="/wiki/All-4-One" title="All-4-One">All-4-One</a>'s ballad "<a href="/wiki/I_Turn_to_You_(All-4-One_song)#Christina_Aguilera_version" title="I Turn to You (All-4-One song)">I Turn to You</a>" is a <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a>-influenced track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBTrackByTrack_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBTrackByTrack-17">[17]</a></sup> On the song, Aguilera thanks someone for their "faith, strength, support, commitment and tenderness."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pluggedin_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-pluggedin-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>"So Emotional", "Love for All Seasons" and "Somebody's Somebody" incorporate strong elements of R&amp;B and soul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IdoReview_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-IdoReview-19">[19]</a></sup> "So Emotional" is a midtempo <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a>-inspired number talking about a man who has got Aguilera "on the ropes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBTrackByTrack_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-BBTrackByTrack-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sonicnews_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-sonicnews-21">[21]</a></sup> "Love for All Seasons" is a pop track which is musically similar to Carey's "<a href="/wiki/Always_Be_My_Baby" title="Always Be My Baby">Always Be My Baby</a>" (1996), while "Somebody's Somebody", in which Aguilera sings about being secure in one's arms, features <a href="/wiki/Drum_kit" title="Drum kit">drums</a> snap, <a href="/wiki/Bass_(instrument)" title="Bass (instrument)">bass</a> pops, and a gospel <a href="/wiki/Organ_(music)" title="Organ (music)">organ</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(music)" title="Bridge (music)">bridge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBTrackByTrack_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-BBTrackByTrack-17">[17]</a></sup> Aguilera sings about a woman longing to reveal her true self on "<a href="/wiki/Reflection_(song)" title="Reflection (song)">Reflection</a>", which Partridge characterized it as the song that "sums up the album."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBTrackByTrack_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-BBTrackByTrack-17">[17]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Come_On_Over_Baby_(All_I_Want_Is_You)" title="Come On Over Baby (All I Want Is You)">Come On Over Baby (All I Want Is You)</a>" is deemed the most "sexual" track on <i>Christina Aguilera</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>-influenced song which features a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rap_music" title="Rap music">rap</a> verse written by Aguilera herself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTVIndia_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTVIndia-22">[22]</a></sup> "When You Put Your Hands On Me", an R&amp;B song co-written by <a href="/wiki/Robin_Thicke" title="Robin Thicke">Robin Thicke</a>, addresses the alchemy of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">sex</a>: "I just know / when you put your hands on me / I feel sexy / and my body turns to gold."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBTrackByTrack_17-5"><a href="#cite_note-BBTrackByTrack-17">[17]</a></sup> "Blessed" features elements of gospel, while "Love Will Find A Way" features an R&amp;B <a href="/wiki/Groove_(music)" title="Groove (music)">groove</a> and was compared to Carey's songs "<a href="/wiki/Emotions_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Emotions (Mariah Carey song)">Emotions</a>" (1991) and "<a href="/wiki/Dreamlover_(song)" title="Dreamlover (song)">Dreamlover</a>" (1993).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IdoReview_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-IdoReview-19">[19]</a></sup> On the final song, "Obvious", Aguilera wonders whether her confusion about her life is apparent to everyone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBTrackByTrack_17-6"><a href="#cite_note-BBTrackByTrack-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christina_Aguilera_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="2.5/5 stars"><img alt="2.5/5 stars" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" <td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Sputnikmusic" title="Sputnikmusic">Sputnikmusic</a></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="3.5/5 stars"><img alt="3.5/5 stars" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Star_half.svg/11px-Star_half.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Star_half.svg/17px-Star_half.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Star_half.svg/22px-Star_half.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sput_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-sput-28">[28]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> praised the songwriting and the "clean and uncluttered" production on the project. He eventually commended on Aguilera's vocals, writing that "she not only has charisma, she can actually sing, bringing conviction to these love and heartbreak songs."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusicreview_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicreview-13">[13]</a></sup> Although calling it "a frustratingly erratic album", Beth Johnson wrote that "Christina still makes a credible bid to be the late-summer soundtrack to romantic rebound."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-EW-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sputnikmusic" title="Sputnikmusic">Sputnikmusic</a> editor Amanda Murray wrote that <i>Christina Aguilera</i> "is an album that is highly representative of the better aspects of the teen pop movement of the late 90s."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sput_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-sput-28">[28]</a></sup> A reviewer writing for <i><a href="/wiki/Q_(magazine)" title="Q (magazine)">Q</a></i> said the album "shows off her pretty, but powerful vocals to surprisingly impressive effect."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-q_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-q-25">[25]</a></sup> Ann Powers on behalf of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> agreed, writing "Beyond its sleek design, this album hints at a real singer's emergence. She has striking vocal power and range, if not a clue about expressing individuality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimesReview_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimesReview-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Barry Walters from <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> criticized the album's theme, calling it "bubble-brained", writing that they "give Aguilera little substance to spin into gold."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-RS-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> stated the album "was avoidance-like LeAnn and unlike Britney, Christina already has 'adult' grit and phrasing down pat, and so threatens to join Gloria, Mariah, Celine, and LeAnn herself in the endless parade of Diane Warren-fueled divas-by-fiat hitting high notes and signifying less than nothing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gau_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-gau-23">[23]</a></sup> Julene Snyder of Sonicnet wrote that "Aguilera has an instinctive grasp of the insipid state of the pop/ dance music scene, especially as it relates to her peers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sonic.net_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-sonic.net-27">[27]</a></sup> On behalf of <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a>, Nikki Tranter said "there are lots of 'oohs' and plenty of 'ahhs' and just enough 'I wants' and 'you likes' to keep the kids happy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popmatters_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-popmatters-14">[14]</a></sup> Partridge deemed the project "quite listenable"; however, he said the lyrics "tell us precious little about the girl on the cover."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBTrackByTrack_17-8"><a href="#cite_note-BBTrackByTrack-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christina_Aguilera_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the United States, <i>Christina Aguilera</i> debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with first-week sales of 252,800, beating <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Puff Daddy</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Forever_(Puff_Daddy_album)" title="Forever (Puff Daddy album)">Forever</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debutalbum_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-debutalbum-29">[29]</a></sup> In its second week, it fell to number 2, selling 218,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The album was <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">certified octuple platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) for exceeding shipments of eight million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAcert_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAcert-31">[31]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>, the release has sold 8,279,000 copies in the U.S. as of September 2014 and is among the most certified albums of all time according to the RIAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_sales_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_sales-32">[a]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> Meanwhile, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BMG_Music" title="BMG Music">BMG Music</a> calculated that <i>Christina Aguilera</i> has sold an additional 935,000 units through BMG Music Clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMG_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-BMG-34">[33]</a></sup> The project also peaked atop the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_charts_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_charts-35">[34]</a></sup> In July 2001, <a href="/wiki/Music_Canada" title="Music Canada">Music Canada</a> certified the project six times <a href="/wiki/List_of_music_recording_certifications" title="List of music recording certifications">platinum</a> for exceeding sales of over 600,000 units in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MusicCanadaii_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-MusicCanadaii-36">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United Kingdom, the album debuted at number 21 on October 30, 1999,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukdebut_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukdebut-37">[36]</a></sup> falling to number 31 the following week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> It stayed two weeks inside the top-forty and only re-entered on February 26, 2000, at number 33.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> The album climbed to number 14 on March 3, 2000, becoming its peak position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> The album stayed on the UK charts for 26 weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukcharts_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukcharts-41">[40]</a></sup> The album was certified <a href="/wiki/List_of_music_recording_certifications" title="List of music recording certifications">platinum</a> by the IFPI for sales of one million copies in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, the album debuted at number 31 on February 20, 2000, while peaking at number 26 two weeks later, spending 15 weeks on the charts. However, the album re-entered at number 25, on October 29, 2000, and two weeks later, it reached a new position of number 21, spending 13 further weeks on the charts, bringing a total of 28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_charts_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA_charts-43">[42]</a></sup> It was later certified platinum for 70,000 sales in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, the album debuted at number 38, on October 31, 1999, and later climbed to number 27, before re-entering two times, on November 28, 1999 and February 13, 2000. After the latter re-entering, the album peaked six weeks later at number 5, on March 26, 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIANZ_charts_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIANZ_charts-45">[44]</a></sup> It re-entered an additional six times and was certified platinum in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, selling over 15,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> The album sold 80,000 copies in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MusicBrazil_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-MusicBrazil-47">[46]</a></sup> As of 2016, <i>Christina Aguilera</i> has sold over 20 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Xtinadebutsales_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Xtinadebutsales-48">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christina_Aguilera_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Genie_in_a_Bottle" title="Genie in a Bottle">Genie in a Bottle</a>" was the first single of the album, released on June 22, 1999. The song received generally favorable reviews from music critics, who commended the song for being pleasant,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sput_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-sput-28">[28]</a></sup> sweet, the album's best moment and her signature track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sonic.net_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-sonic.net-27">[27]</a></sup> It became one of Aguilera's highest charting singles, getting certified platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a>. The song became an overnight hit, making it Aguilera's first number one single. It topped the charts for five weeks straight on <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 due to strong physical CD sales and airplay, having the longest stay at number one that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardmagazine_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboardmagazine-49">[48]</a></sup> The single made airplay history, becoming one of the most successful airplay-only singles and topped the charts weeks before an accompanying music video was made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusicgenie_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicgenie-50">[49]</a></sup> It also topped the charts of eight countries, while it charted within the top five in every country it was released in.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> Its music video was a success, becoming a staple on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">Total Request Live</a> with Aguilera enjoying some fun and sexual tension at a beach bonfire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-axs_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-axs-52">[51]</a></sup> The song received a Grammy Nomination for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a>. A version of the song in Spanish entitled "Genio Atrapado" was recorded and included in some editions of <i>Christina Aguilera</i> and later on her Spanish-language album, <i><a href="/wiki/Mi_Reflejo" title="Mi Reflejo">Mi Reflejo</a></i> and peaked at number 13 on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Latin_Songs" title="Hot Latin Songs"><i>Billboard</i> Hot Latin Songs</a> chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latinsongs_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-latinsongs-53">[52]</a></sup> It also received a <a href="/wiki/Latin_Grammy_Award" title="Latin Grammy Award">Latin Grammy Award</a> nomination for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_Grammy_Awards_of_2000" title="Latin Grammy Awards of 2000">1st Latin Grammy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:What_A_Girl_Wants122_-_CA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/What_A_Girl_Wants122_-_CA.jpg/170px-What_A_Girl_Wants122_-_CA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/What_A_Girl_Wants122_-_CA.jpg/255px-What_A_Girl_Wants122_-_CA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/What_A_Girl_Wants122_-_CA.jpg/340px-What_A_Girl_Wants122_-_CA.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:What_A_Girl_Wants122_-_CA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aguilera performing "What a Girl Wants" during her <a href="/wiki/Back_to_Basics_Tour" title="Back to Basics Tour">Back to Basics Tour</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/What_a_Girl_Wants_(Christina_Aguilera_song)" title="What a Girl Wants (Christina Aguilera song)">What a Girl Wants</a>" was the second single from the album. Instead of the slower version, Aguilera insisted that a more upbeat mix, with an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> edge, needed to be created to be released as a single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-top10about.com_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-top10about.com-55">[54]</a></sup> Released on October 29, 1999 to radio stations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whatagirlwantsrelease_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-whatagirlwantsrelease-56">[55]</a></sup> the song received positive reviews from critics, with most praising her vocals in the track,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> comparing to those of <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-ref-4">[4]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sonic.net_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-sonic.net-27">[27]</a></sup> "What a Girl Wants" peaked at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 on January 15, 2000 for two weeks, ending the chart reign of <a href="/wiki/Santana_(band)" title="Santana (band)">Santana</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Smooth_(song)" title="Smooth (song)">Smooth</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> and becoming Aguilera's second number-one single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardmagazine_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboardmagazine-49">[48]</a></sup> The single also topped the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish charts</a>, while also peaking at number three in the UK, at number five in Australia and reached the top-twenty in most countries it charted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> The song was nominated for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/43rd_Grammy_Awards" title="43rd Grammy Awards">43rd Grammy Awards</a> held on February 21, 2001. A Spanish version entitled "Una Mujer" was also made and included on <i>Mi Reflejo</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mireflejo_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-mireflejo-60">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I_Turn_to_You_(Christina_Aguilera_song)#Christina_Aguilera_version" title="I Turn to You (Christina Aguilera song)">I Turn to You</a>" was the third single form the album, released on April 1, 2000 to U.S radio. It received mixed reviews from critics, who recognized that the track allowed Aguilera's vocals to soar and shine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sput_28-3"><a href="#cite_note-sput-28">[28]</a></sup> but called it a cliché ballad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> However, the single peaked at number 3 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 for 4 weeks, becoming Aguilera's third top-ten hit. The single also reached the top-ten in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canada_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-canada-62">[61]</a></sup> the top-twenty in other three countries, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK" title="UK">UK</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukcharts_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-ukcharts-41">[40]</a></sup> and the top-forty elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> The music video was directed by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kahn" title="Joseph Kahn">Joseph Kahn</a>, and Christina is seen singing in front of a microphone before walking in the rain with an umbrella, and on a rooftop. The video's storyline follows a young woman getting into an accident, with her mother worriedly waiting for word on where she is at the late hour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celebritycafe_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-celebritycafe-64">[63]</a></sup> A Spanish version entitled "Por Siempre Tu" was released and included on her Spanish-debut album, <i>Mi Reflejo</i>. It peaked at number 6 on the Hot Latin Songs chart, becoming Aguilera's first top-ten Spanish single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latinsongs_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-latinsongs-53">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 27, 2000, during an interview with <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jam!_Canoe" title="Jam! Canoe">Jam! Canoe</a>'</i>s Stephanie McGrath, Aguilera revealed plans to release at least two more singles from her debut: "So Emotional" in the fall and "Come On Over" as soon as "I Turn To You", "runs its toll," she said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jam_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-jam-8">[8]</a></sup> "So Emotional" indeed had a simple music video, which was available through her <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VEVO" title="VEVO">VEVO</a> account,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> showing Christina in a casual outfit recording the song in the studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celebritycafe2_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-celebritycafe2-66">[65]</a></sup> However, the song was never released and "Come on Over" was chosen instead. For the song's release, Aguilera claimed: "We're going to head back in the studio, give it more of an edge, R&amp;B it up a little, maybe rock it out a little, give it a lot of different new directions and get it out there."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jam_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-jam-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The re-worked version, entitled "<a href="/wiki/Come_On_Over_Baby_(All_I_Want_Is_You)" title="Come On Over Baby (All I Want Is You)">Come on Over Baby (All I Want Is You)</a>", features more <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance</a> elements as well as "edgy" and "sexual" lyrics,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-top10about.com_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-top10about.com-55">[54]</a></sup> even a rap by Aguilera, and was released on September 26, 2000 as the album's fourth and final single. The song's new version received mixed reviews, with some criticizing the fact that the track "was more like an album track than a hit", but praised the catchy chorus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> However, the song was a success on the charts, becoming Aguilera's third number-one hit on the U.S. <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 chart, spending four weeks at the top, from October 8 to November 4, 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardmagazine_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-billboardmagazine-49">[48]</a></sup> It spent twenty-one weeks on the Hot 100, ranked thirty-eight on the Hot 100's 2000 Year-end charts and eventually the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RIAA" title="RIAA">RIAA</a> certified the single gold. It was also a success elsewhere, reaching the top-ten in over six countries, including Australia, Canada and the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukcharts_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-ukcharts-41">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> The video was considered "bright and colorful," with green, white, and gold backgrounds juxtaposed against a dance choreography.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celebritycafe3_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-celebritycafe3-69">[68]</a></sup> A Spanish version entitled "Ven Conmigo (Solamente Tú)" became a number-one hit on the Hot Latin Songs chart, becoming her first Spanish chart topper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latinsongs_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-latinsongs-53">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christina_Aguilera_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Aguilera made many appearances on talk shows in order to promote her self-titled debut album. Aguilera appeared on shows such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rosie_O%27Donnell_Show" title="The Rosie O'Donnell Show">The Rosie O'Donnell Show</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">TRL</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> Aguilera also began traveling to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> while "What a Girl Wants" was topping the charts overseas. In 1999, Aguilera performed "Genie in a Bottle" at the 1999 <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Awards" title="Teen Choice Awards">Teen Choice Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> Aguilera also attended the <a href="/wiki/2000_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2000 MTV Video Music Awards">2000 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, where she and Fred Durst performed together. Aguilera performed "Come on Over Baby", wearing a tight ruby red outfit with black and red streaks in her hair, and near the end, Durst walked onstage and performed part of his band's song "Livin' It Up" with Aguilera. After eliciting charged reactions from his fans, Durst stated: "I already told you guys before, I did it all for the nookie, man."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> The feud died weeks later, when Aguilera denied Durst's statement, saying Durst "got no nookie."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> Later on, in 2000, Aguilera performed at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXIV" title="Super Bowl XXXIV">Super Bowl XXXIV</a> as a halftime performer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jam_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-jam-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 1999, Aguilera issued a full-length home video titled <i><a href="/wiki/Genie_Gets_Her_Wish" title="Genie Gets Her Wish">Genie Gets Her Wish</a></i>. The video includes interviews with her from backstage, in the studio and on the road. It also features Aguilera's rendition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mel_Torme" title="Mel Torme">Mel Torme</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuletide" title="Yuletide">Yuletide</a> classic "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Christmas_Song_(Chestnuts_Roasting_on_an_Open_Fire)" title="The Christmas Song (Chestnuts Roasting on an Open Fire)">The Christmas Song (Chestnuts Roasting on an Open Fire)</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sonicnews_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-sonicnews-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Touring">Touring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christina_Aguilera_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Touring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera_in_Concert" title="Christina Aguilera in Concert">Christina Aguilera in Concert</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stripped_Tour_-_Genie_in_a_Bottle.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Stripped_Tour_-_Genie_in_a_Bottle.jpg/170px-Stripped_Tour_-_Genie_in_a_Bottle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Stripped_Tour_-_Genie_in_a_Bottle.jpg/255px-Stripped_Tour_-_Genie_in_a_Bottle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Stripped_Tour_-_Genie_in_a_Bottle.jpg/340px-Stripped_Tour_-_Genie_in_a_Bottle.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stripped_Tour_-_Genie_in_a_Bottle.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aguilera performing "Genie in a Bottle" on her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stripped_World_Tour" title="Stripped World Tour">Stripped World Tour</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On April 28, 2000, Aguilera announced her first tour, whick kicked off on July 31, 2000 and would hit 37 cities (and a total of 81 shows). The tour was sponsored by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sears,_Roebuck_and_Company" title="Sears, Roebuck and Company">Sears</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levi%27s" title="Levi's">Levi's</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvtour_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvtour-75">[74]</a></sup> Aguilera released a statement about the tour, saying: "Headlining my own tour means creative control and a high-energy, let-loose show. It's designed with my band and dancers to be a visually exciting mix of my big hits and some special surprises," said Christina. "Plus, my sponsors, Sears and Levi's, are giving fans lots of ways to get involved with the tour, like exclusive CDs and posters, a chance to win a backstage pass to hang with me and a cause-related program called 'Come On Over and Do Something' that was created specifically for the tour."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> About the tour's setlist, she claimed, "I'll be doing songs from my debut album. But I've changed so much from doing that at 17, so we'll put a whole new twist on things from my album. … There will be a lot of blues and soul inflections, which is what I've wanted to do more of for a long time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvtour_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtvtour-75">[74]</a></sup> One feature of the shows she described involved getting the crowd excited with her hit "What a Girl Wants" and then switching to a piano-and-vocal-only song by her hero, blues legend <a href="/wiki/Etta_James" title="Etta James">Etta James</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvtour_75-2"><a href="#cite_note-mtvtour-75">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christina_Aguilera_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Aguilera was nominated for two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a> in 2000: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_New_Artist" title="Best New Artist">Best New Artist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a> for "<a href="/wiki/Genie_in_a_Bottle" title="Genie in a Bottle">Genie in a Bottle</a>", with Aguilera winning the first.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> Jason Lipshutz of <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> cited her win on the Grammy as one of her "10 Biggest Career Moments", claiming: "The battle for teen pop supremacy made its way to the Grammy Awards in 2000, when <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> and Christina Aguilera were both nominated for the Best New Artist prize. Both singing stars had issued hit albums in 1999, […] and Aguilera ended up walking away with one of the night's top prizes. "I'm shaking right now!" Aguilera told the audience at the 2000 ceremony, also admitting that she did not have a speech prepared for the event because she didn't think she would win. Aguilera has since taken home three more Grammys, for the songs '<a href="/wiki/Lady_Marmalade" title="Lady Marmalade">Lady Marmalade</a>,' '<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_(Christina_Aguilera_song)" title="Beautiful (Christina Aguilera song)">Beautiful</a>' and '<a href="/wiki/Ain%27t_No_Other_Man" title="Ain't No Other Man">Ain't No Other Man</a>," respectively."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> Aguilera also received another Grammy nomination in 2001 for "<a href="/wiki/What_a_Girl_Wants_(Christina_Aguilera_song)" title="What a Girl Wants (Christina Aguilera song)">What a Girl Wants</a>" on the "Best Female Pop Vocal Performance" category, and according to <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i>, "both of which helped catapult the album to the top of the charts."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timebio_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-timebio-79">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aguilera's Grammy Award nominations, two back to back number-one singles, magazine gossip, and merchandise released under her name made her the "It girl", according to <i>People</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uncorking_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-uncorking-80">[79]</a></sup> In March 2000, <a href="/wiki/Lori_Majewski" title="Lori Majewski">Lori Majewski</a>, entertainment director at <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teen_People" title="Teen People">Teen People</a></i> magazine, stated: "If people want to know why Christina is going to be around a decade from now, the answer is very clear: It's pure talent," Majewski said. "When you hear this girl open her mouth, everyone is astounded. I've seen her sing many times, and every time, I'm impressed, but the people who are hearing it for the first time can't even believe it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> In an article about the "2013 Most Influential People in the World", in which Aguilera appeared, Canadian singer-songwriter <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%A9line_Dion" title="Céline Dion">Céline Dion</a> claimed that, "I remember she broke onto the scene at the turn of the millennium, […] so I got to watch a lot of her TV appearances, especially on the award shows. I remember thinking, This girl's got it all and then some! Unbelievable voice, great dancer and so very beautiful."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time100_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-time100-82">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The songs on the album played important roles on Aguilera's legacy. "<a href="/wiki/Genie_in_a_Bottle" title="Genie in a Bottle">Genie in a Bottle</a>", the album's lead-single, was a number-one hit and Aguilera became the third female artist in 1999 to top the Hot 100 chart with her debut entry, behind Britney Spears's "<a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)" title="...Baby One More Time (song)">...Baby One More Time</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/If_You_Had_My_Love" title="If You Had My Love">If You Had My Love</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-axs_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-axs-52">[51]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">Allmusic</a></i> highlighted that the single incredibly hit number-one on the Billboard's Hot 100 chart before a music video was even out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusicgenie_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicgenie-50">[49]</a></sup> "Genie" was listed at number 38 on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s 100 Greatest Songs of the 90s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/About.com" title="About.com">About.com</a> placed it at number 2 on her "Top 10 Songs",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-top10about.com_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-top10about.com-55">[54]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/AOL_Radio" title="AOL Radio">AOL Radio</a> ranked at number-one, calling it her "<a href="/wiki/Signature_song" title="Signature song">signature song</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aol_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-aol-84">[83]</a></sup> While listing the "100 Greatest Singers of All Time", <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a> placed Aguilera at number 52, picking "Genie in a Bottle" as one of her "key tracks", writing that "Even in her teen-pop 'Genie in a Bottle' days, she was modeling her dramatic, melismatic technique on old-school soul heroines like Etta James."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-rs-85">[84]</a></sup> It was also the top selling debut single of 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DebutSingle_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-DebutSingle-86">[85]</a></sup> The song was also covered by contestants of many popular talent shows such as <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_9)" title="American Idol (season 9)">American Idol</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor" title="The X Factor">The X Factor</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._season_5)" title="The Voice (U.S. season 5)">The Voice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> The success of the follow-up single "<a href="/wiki/What_a_Girl_Wants_(Christina_Aguilera_song)" title="What a Girl Wants (Christina Aguilera song)">What a Girl Wants</a>" solidified her as a strong musical force and earned her several accolades, including five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a> nominations and a Grammy Award nomination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aol_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-aol-84">[83]</a></sup> The song's title inspired the title of 2000's American <a href="/wiki/Romantic_comedy_film" title="Romantic comedy film">romantic comedy film</a> "<a href="/wiki/What_Women_Want" title="What Women Want">What Women Want</a>", having the track on its soundtrack<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> and on a scene.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avclub_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-avclub-90">[89]</a></sup> It also inspired the title of the 2003 comedy <a href="/wiki/What_a_Girl_Wants_(film)" title="What a Girl Wants (film)">film of the same name</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/I_Turn_to_You_(All-4-One_song)#Christina_Aguilera_version" title="I Turn to You (All-4-One song)">I Turn to You</a>" inspired American recording artist <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>, as she stated, "When I was 15, I was singing 'I Turn to You' at the top of my lungs trying to hit all her notes. So she was an inspiration to me to have a wider vocal range."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> With the album's fourth single, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Come_on_Over_Baby_(All_I_Want_Is_You)" title="Come on Over Baby (All I Want Is You)">Come on Over Baby (All I Want Is You)</a>", Aguilera managed to have three number-one singles for the same album and four top-ten singles, an achievement she only did with her first album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardmagazine_49-3"><a href="#cite_note-billboardmagazine-49">[48]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christina_Aguilera_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-US_sales-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-US_sales_32-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-US_sales_32-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">As of September 2014, <i>Christina Aguilera</i> has sold 8,279,000 copies in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2014_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014-119">[118]</a></sup> The aforementioned sales figures are combined by <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>, which does not count albums sold through clubs as does <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BMG_Music_Service" title="BMG Music Service">BMG Music Service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> According to BMG Music Service, the album has additionally sold 935,000 copies at BMG Music Clubs as of 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
